## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: thermomechanical constitutive modeling (materials science)
**Analysis**: This task models the stress-strain-temperature relationship in materials. Temperature typically modifies elastic stiffness and flow stress, while strain determines the deformation response through linear or nonlinear constitutive laws.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Hooke's Law (temperature-dependent): sigma = c0 * epsilon (linear elasticity at fixed T)
- Temperature-dependent elastic modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T) * epsilon (linear modulus variation with T)
- Exponential thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * T) (thermally-activated softening)
- Power-law hardening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 (nonlinear strain hardening, Ramberg-Osgood type)
- Power-law hardening with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * exp(c2 * T) (combined hardening and thermal effects)
- Johnson-Cook type (simplified): sigma = (c0 + c1 * epsilon**c2) * (c3 + c4 * T) (strain hardening with linear thermal softening)
- Ludwik-Hollomon with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon**c1 * T**c2 (power-law coupling of strain and temperature)
- Voce hardening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) (saturating strain hardening)
- Voce with thermal softening: sigma = c0 * (1 - exp(c1 * epsilon)) * exp(c2 * T) (saturating hardening + thermal effect)
- Polynomial modulus: sigma = (c0 + c1 * T + c2 * T**2) * epsilon (quadratic temperature dependence of modulus)
- Arrhenius-type thermal factor: sigma = c0 * epsilon * exp(c1 * (c2 - T)**(-1)) (thermally-activated deformation)
- Swift hardening with temperature: sigma = c0 * (epsilon + c1)**c2 * (c3 + c4 * T) (offset power-law with thermal factor)
- Hyperbolic tangent hardening: sigma = c0 * tanh(c1 * epsilon) * (c2 + c3 * T) (saturating flow stress with thermal softening)
- Bilinear with temperature: sigma = c0 * epsilon * (c1 + c2 * T) + c3 * epsilon**2 (quadratic strain with thermal coupling)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Temperature-dependent stiffness → Multiplicative separation: f(epsilon) * g(T), where g(T) is a softening function
- Strain hardening saturation → (1 - exp(-c*epsilon)) or tanh(c*epsilon) captures diminishing hardening rate
- Power-law strain hardening → epsilon**c with 0 < c < 1 represents work hardening in metals (Hollomon relation)
- Linear thermal softening → Factor (1 - c*T) or (c0 + c1*T) with c1 < 0 for decreasing modulus with temperature
- Multiplicative decomposition of stress → sigma = H(epsilon) * S(T) where H is hardening and S is thermal softening, reflecting separable physics
- Offset strain for pre-existing hardening → (epsilon + c)**n instead of epsilon**n avoids singularity at zero strain (Swift model)
- Arrhenius temperature sensitivity → exp(-c/T) appears when thermally-activated dislocation mechanisms dominate
- Concavity change in stress-strain curve → Transition from hardening to softening may require rational forms or competing exponentials

## Analysis

The Ground Truth expression is:
$$f(\epsilon, T) = 55.83\epsilon(-0.0970(T - 325.31) + 1) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T - 325.31)^2)$$

Expanding the first part:
$$f(\epsilon, T) = 55.83\epsilon \cdot (-0.0970T + 0.0970 \cdot 325.31 + 1) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$
$$= \epsilon(-5.414T + 32.54) + 6.648\epsilon \exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$

So the GT is essentially:
$$f(\epsilon, T) = \epsilon(a \cdot T + b) + c \cdot \epsilon \cdot \exp(-(T - d)^2)$$

The key structural feature is:
1. A term linear in both $\epsilon$ and $T$
2. A constant term proportional to $\epsilon$
3. A **Gaussian in T** multiplied by $\epsilon$

The critical component is the Gaussian $\exp(-(T-d)^2)$ multiplied by $\epsilon$. Let me check each candidate for the ability to produce this Gaussian term.

Most candidates contain terms like:
- `sin(T*c + c)` — sinusoidal, not Gaussian
- `log(...)` — logarithmic, not Gaussian
- `exp(c*epsilon)` or `exp(c*epsilon**2)` — exponential in epsilon, not T
- Rational functions of epsilon — not Gaussian in T
- `exp(c*sin(T*c + c))` — not a Gaussian in T

**Candidate 21**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2/(c3 + epsilon) + T*c4*epsilon**2 + c5 + c6*epsilon*exp(c7/(-T + c8))`

This has `epsilon*exp(c7/(-T + c8))` which is $\epsilon \exp\left(\frac{c_7}{c_8 - T}\right)$. This is a reciprocal exponential, not a Gaussian $\exp(-(T-d)^2)$. Not equivalent.

**Candidate 38**: Has `epsilon*exp(c8/(-T + c9))` — same issue, not Gaussian.

**Candidate 26**: `T*c0*epsilon + T*c1 + T*c2/(c3 + epsilon) + c4*epsilon*exp(c5/(T + c6)) + c7*exp(c8*epsilon**2)` — has `epsilon*exp(c5/(T+c6))`, again not Gaussian in T.

**Candidate 37**: Has `exp(T*c7)*log(c8*epsilon + 1)` — exponential in T, not Gaussian.

None of the candidates contain a term of the form $\epsilon \cdot \exp(-(T - c)^2)$ or anything that could algebraically reduce to a Gaussian in T. The exponential terms in the candidates are either:
- Exponentials of $\epsilon$ (not T)
- Exponentials of $1/(T-c)$ (poles, not Gaussian)
- Exponentials of $T$ (exponential growth, not Gaussian)
- Exponentials of trigonometric functions of T

None of these can reproduce the Gaussian $\exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$ behavior for all values of T.

Conclusion: No match

## Ground Truth Analysis

The GT is:
$$f(\epsilon, T) = 55.831574\cdot\epsilon\cdot(-0.09696(T - 325.31) + 1) + \epsilon\cdot 6.648\cdot\exp(-(T - 325.31)^2)$$

Expanding the first term:
$$= 55.831574\cdot\epsilon\cdot(-0.09696\cdot T + 0.09696\cdot 325.31 + 1) + 6.648\cdot\epsilon\cdot\exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$
$$= -5.414\cdot\epsilon\cdot T + 55.831574\cdot\epsilon\cdot(1 + 31.539) + 6.648\cdot\epsilon\cdot\exp(-(T-325.31)^2)$$

So GT = $a\cdot\epsilon\cdot T + b\cdot\epsilon + c\cdot\epsilon\cdot\exp(-(T-d)^2)$

where $a \approx -5.414$, $b \approx 55.831574 \times 32.539 \approx 1816.7$, $c \approx 6.648$, $d \approx 325.31$.

The key structural features of GT:
1. A term linear in $\epsilon \cdot T$
2. A term linear in $\epsilon$
3. A Gaussian term in T multiplied by $\epsilon$: $\epsilon \cdot \exp(-(T-d)^2)$

**Everything is proportional to $\epsilon$.** There are no terms independent of $\epsilon$, no terms with $1/(c+\epsilon)$, no polynomial terms in $\epsilon^2$, no $\sin$ functions, no $\log$ functions.
